< Review>
My second favorite place to surf in Santa Cruz. I came here as a beginner which was a mistake there is a lot of localism. That said if you have decent skills the waves are nice and the area is really cool. The hike down from the bluff makes you feel like you're going on an adventure. There isn't much parking nearby but I managed to find a spot.<//Review>

Good pizza here. At least as good as an equally expensive place out in Yorba Linda off YL blvd at Yorba Ranch. < Text>
Beautiful, glassy slabs that never seem to quit. I stopped by to watch the surfers on my way south to SD and ended up staying a couple of hours. There's a certain quality of the waves here that's hard to describe. They're slower moving than the waves I'm used to in SoCal and they maintain their shape very well. Can't wait to try my hand at surfing here someday.</Text>

< Text>
June 14th and Rincon Beach was 100% filled with RVs. Rincon is fun if you don't have a place to park near the ocean. Almost no facilities accept an occasion loud house but lots of ocean. If you need more facilities many of these small parks along Rincon have more complete setups. Spaces are first come first serve along Rincon Beach but reservations are necessity for any of the small parks. Steel Rangers to pay at Rincon attendance to pay at the parks.
Rincon is a fun experience if you haven't camped right along the Pacific Ocean before< /Text>

<text>They answer their phones promptly and are knowledgeable about the subject. I needed my prints taken to get my identity history report from the FBI and the person I spoke to over the phone was aware of the FBI's new processing changes; so they stay up to date on their information.

The visit was quick, as soon as you walk in someone asks what service you are there for and it's all hands on deck, everyone in the office helps. The staff is friendly and efficient.

They provided the finger print card, and all the labels and envelopes needed to complete my order with the FBI. When I called my local police dept. to get my prints taken there they said I needed to provide my own fingerprint card, which I wouldn't know where to get except print a copy from the internet on normal paper. But this place had actual print cards on thick paper and cut into the correct square size. They provided everything.

They advised me over the phone what paperwork the FBI needed included in the envelope to complete my order. I took that paperwork in when I went for my prints and after they put together all my paperwork in a legal sized envelope with a pre printed label all I had to do was drop it off at the post office. They made the service fast and easy. I would definitely recommend coming here for any live scan/fingerprint services and I would return if I needed any of these services in the future.< /text>< Pictures>

<rating>5</rating><Review>Had a wonderful experience here at Wa Dining Okan. Luckily, we got there right when they opened, so all their tables were open; mind you, the place is quite small and has about 3 four person tables and 2-3 two person tables, alongside their bar which fits around 15.

The food was superb, they did a fantastic job at making our time here enjoyable and refreshing. We tried different meal choices we haven't had before and instead of being typical flavors you've had elsewhere, they really did come with new tastes. The food being cooked perfectly and their menu having a good variety made us feel welcomed to eat at a restaurant of a different nationality. They also didn't have any issues with explanations or understanding of our questions, which was great.

The waitresses were quick to serve and were professional. I noticed how often they checked in on their customers without being obnoxious. Always seemed to come at the right time.

The price was about what I expected going in (above average), so if you plan on eating cheap, just get one of their regular entree meals. That being said, $80 (tip included) was great to see for how much we ordered, making it well worth it.

One of my only cons, which isn't their fault, is that the building since being small, only has one restroom. Keep this in mind if you are someone that needs to use it often, so you can go next door without feeling awkward.

Overall, I had a terrific experience and would recommend this place to anyone looking for Japanese food that isn't just sushi.</Review><pictures>None</pictures>< resp>

<review>Sometimes I feel this place is a hidden gem.  It's in the corner, it's very small and intimate inside.  It's authentic Japanese food.  Go for dinner.  The lunch menu is very limiting.  For dinner, we had the grilled whole squid.  F***ing amazing.  Sashimi bowl is AMAZING, flavorful, exquisite and fresh.  Karaage chicken is very good.  Friend baby octopus for lunch was a little too greasy/oily since the octopus holds the deep fry oil.  Tonkotsu Ramen is really good.  For lunch, the Miso Mackerel was delightful and strong in flavor.  Get there early or get there knowing there's going to be a wait.  Well worth it though.  Parking like most of Kearny is going to be a cluster F...  but again... worth it.  Lol.  hope this review helped!  Like it if it did.<//review>< pictures>

<Rate>5<//Rate><Text>This restaurant really reminded me of my (short) trip to Japan. It's a tiny little spot that probably only holds about twenty people or so max. It's dominated by a three-sided-bar in the center of the room, which is a great place to sit. They have some of the specials set out around the bar so you can see what you'd be getting.

The food is fantastic here. The flavor is great and there are unique choices. However, the portions are on the smaller side and the prices are on the higher side. I have never felt ripped off here though and have always left happy. Just keep it in mind that you will not be having a cheap meal and you'll be fine.</Text><Pictures>None< /Pictures><response>None</response>< GmapID>

< review>
Cozy/Cute Japanese food restaurant / Good food / Okay Price / Mean Waitress

I went to this place at lunch time.
The waitress was non-friendly and rude. I want to say 4 stars for their Food/Price but that's because we had bad experience at this time by waitress, I'm rating 2 stars for her service.

We was with toddlers and when they found that my friend was feeding her toddler (1yr old) his food, waitress came up to our table and told us that we can't do that. (You cannot bring food from outside)
And she told us that we have to purchase their food and offer us white plain rice.
Was she really telling us to feed our kids just white rice?
If they had at leaset kids meal to offer but still.
Some kids have to follow their special diet but they still have the right to enjoy their meal at the same table with us. Right?

I thought the store policy doesn't make any sense. And I know the waitress was just following her company. But she could tell us nicely. Not like Oh no you're breaking-the-law! attitude.

For the owner. Please fix your non-kids-friendly rule or just put "No Kids" sign in the front.
How does that look?<//review>

<gmap_id>0x80dbffe914a030af:0x73ecda0c2837e7be</gmap_id><Time>1451368034295</Time><username>Russell Delarosa</username><userid>109218867154775676122< /userid></record></dataset><record>
< Review>
Okan was okay, but one dish carried the entire experience: the Kama Eel (rice with eel). This alone would be worth a repeat visit: rich, gorgeous mouthfeel, delicious, satisfying. The rest of the meal was only so-so. The sashimi platter was fresh, but not memorable. The kobe beef appetizer was good, but only somewhat memorable, with the onions underneath providing a nice crunch and textural contrast to the very good beef. The black sesame ice cream was almost under-sweet. I like a dessert that isn't saccharine, but this one needed something to raise it a notch or two. The molasses pudding was like a creme brulee without the topping, which sounds good but it was also only okay. Overall the meal was average for the area, but that Kama eel rice, oh man. I could eat that for days.</Review>

Ashley Qu< /name>
< Text>
Authentic Japanese food with decently quick service.

For lunch, always bring cash. They offer bento boxes that are delicious, and you can have many alternatives, especially their rice options! I highly recommend the Salmon Rice Bowl, if you get the chance. Fresh and delicious. Their noodles are awesome too.

Dinner has the best options for food, especially the small octopi dish. Though these little creatures may seem intimidating at first, they are delicious and I always order this dish. I highly recommend the desserts, especially the black pudding. Definitely a place to reset/cleanse your palette if you've been consuming too much fatty foods lately.< /Text>

What a hidden jewel in San Diego. And by the size of the restaurant, they don't bother flaunting their quality. Quite cheap Japanese tapa-style food with the best quality ever. We had a miso-paste eggplants which were perfect. Had some beef-tongue skewers, again, perfectly cooked and glazed on the outside. And then the highlight - salmon and salmon roe rice... these guys just know how to do it. At this point, I'm convinced that anything they do would be amazing and just wished I hadn't driven so that I can enjoy it with sake next time.< /review>

< Text>
Came here for a quick lunch by myself. There were five other couples here, all speaking Japanese so I felt like I found a good place.

Disclaimer: I do not claim to be an expert on Japanese food, this is my own personal experience.

I ordered the bento box with seared beef, which was diverse and interesting but just wasn't as good as I had hoped for given prior reviews. I'm not sure of I'm just used to different styles of food, but the food wasn't nearly as flavorful as I expected. The miso and potato salads were ok. The beef I thought was 4/5 stars, which was still quite enjoyable.

For desert I got the pudding with black honey, which was good but not the amazingness I expected from the reviews.

Perhaps this place is truly authentic and I'm just not appreciating it, but for my experience I have to give it 4/5 stars overall for lunch.</Text>

<review>Food: Nice change up from the usual Japanese restaurant fare of sushi, ramen, udon and robatayaki.

Some very well executed traditional food to be had here. Today's lunch - braised pork belly with boiled egg, salmon sashimi - both with rice, braised eggplant, and assorted pickles - fried baby octopus, and draft Sapporo.

Ambience: Small, casual, quiet (I did hear some R&B playing in the kitchen).

Service: Polite, efficient.

Easy recommendation if you're in the Kearny Mesa area of San Diego, which is where you want to be when looking for various Asian noms in SD.

Oh, and CASH ONLY.<//review>< pics>

I have been to this nail shop a few times and the result is always sub-par. This last time, about a week ago, I went to have my nails done for a family reunion. I have been eating here for maybe 15 years, since before the name and look changed. It is amazingly deliciouss Mexican food. Always a fun crowd, friendly staff, and they have karaoke some nights. There is a bar side too, if you want a wuick visit on high chairs and small talk.
Great atmosphere always, whether I came by for lunch, or went all put for dinner, joining the party crowds.
If you need a pick-me up day to spoil yourself with good food and good conversation, this is a great place to go. Gas stations on both corners across from it, and an art store, if you are out shopping, or on your way in/out of town.
It is also inside a small business shopping center, so there usually is plenty parking, and even street parking.

<Time>1583304610367</Time><rate>4</rate><Review>I was in the Civic Center area tight on time and looking for a quick bite to eat before seeing Hamilton at the Orpheum Theater. Fortunately, I  happened upon Gyro King, and indeed this restaurant turned out to be the perfect solution! They have a very solid selection of gyro plates and wraps, which also includes a good variety of vegetation selections. The service is relatively quick, since all the food is pre-cooked and they simply need to assemble your plate/wrap before you can dig in and enjoy! The seating inside is a little tight, but I had no problems finding a table and they also offer outside seating if it does get full.

Before I get into the food, I will have to admit that the restaurant's location isn't in the most ideal place. There is a chance one could feel a little cautious eating in this area, but nevertheless it's a solid option for a fast meal in the Civic Area. You definitely can't go wrong with their food!

I ordered the lab and beef gyro plate, which also came with a serving of bread. Luckily, I was particularly hungry on this day or else I don't think I would've been able to finish it all off. They definitely give generous portions, so I hope you're hungry when you visit Gyro King (or at least bring a friend with you to share)!< /Review>< Pics>

< review>
Owners are so helpful, and food is prepared quickly tho it's all made from scratch. Prices are good for SF. Try the gyro or lamb shish-ka-bob. Their appetizer plate and side of hummus are very tasty, bread is fresh and any salad you get is going to be mouth-watering.

I grab my lunch to go often from their for a shift at Bill Graham, I'm often in a rush and I work the late shift from 5p-12p. I grab a combo gyro around 4:45, never have to wait and I'm good for the night. I brought my family in on Monday late afternoon and they really enjoyed it. The kids are sweet fiends do getting them to eat healthy is a chore, but they enjoyed this. We did have a piece of baklava and some rice pudding, it was fabulous.

A must do for anyone, visitor or local alike will truly enjoy the fare and the service.< /review>
